# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# LLVM Pass Manager Registration and Execution Chain

## Your Task

Trace how a new LLVM optimization pass is registered and executed in llvm/llvm-project. Find C++ source files that define: the PassManager template, the PassRegistry, the pass add() registration, and the pass execution order in the standard optimization pipeline (O2/O3).

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d, sg-evals/gcc--96dfb333.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d` (llvm/llvm-project)
- `sg-evals/gcc--96dfb333` (gcc-mirror/gcc)

54-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive answer documenting the LLVM pass manager registration and execution chain. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Files and Concepts:

1. **PassManager Template** (`llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h`, lines 159-226):
   - Generic template that manages a sequence of passes
   - `addPass()` method adds passes to be executed
   - `run()` method executes all passes in sequence

2. **PassRegistry** (`llvm/include/llvm/PassRegistry.h`):
   - Global registry that stores PassInfo objects
   - `registerPass()` registers a pass at startup
   - Maps pass identifiers to PassInfo metadata

3. **Pass Registration** (`llvm/include/llvm/PassSupport.h`):
   - `INITIALIZE_PASS_BEGIN/END` macros automate registration
   - Creates PassInfo objects and registers them with PassRegistry
   - Uses thread-safe `llvm::once_flag` for initialization
   - Example: InstructionCombining.cpp (lines 6331-6343)

4. **Pass Execution** (`llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManagerImpl.h`, lines 27-98):
   - `PassManager::run()` iterates through passes in vector
   - Calls instrumentation callbacks before/after each pass
   - Invalidates analyses based on PreservedAnalyses
   - Returns aggregated analysis preservation info

5. **Pipeline Building** (`llvm/lib/Passes/PassBuilderPipelines.cpp`):
   - `buildModuleOptimizationPipeline()` (lines 1477+): Core O2/O3 module-level optimization order
   - `buildFunctionSimplificationPipeline()` (lines 591+): Function-level simplifications
   - Specific pass ordering includes: SROA → EarlyCSE → InstCombine → AggressiveInstCombine → loop passes → vectorization

6. **Pass Registry Definition** (`llvm/lib/Passes/PassRegistry.def`):
   - Defines all available passes using MODULE_PASS, FUNCTION_PASS macros
   - Entries expanded in PassBuilde
... (truncated)

There\n11: /// is no \"pass\" interface in LLVM per se. Instead, an instance of any class\n12: /// which supports a method to 'run' it over a unit of IR can be used as\n13: /// a pass. A pass manager is generally a tool to collect a sequence of passes\n14: /// which run over a particular IR construct, and run each of them in sequence\n15: /// over each such construct in the containing IR construct. As there is no\n16: /// containing IR construct for a Module, a manager for passes over modules\n17: /// forms the base case which runs its managed passes in sequence over the\n18: /// single module provided.\n19: ///\n20: /// The core IR library provides managers for running passes over\n21: /// modules and functions.\n22: ///\n23: /// * FunctionPassManager can run over a Module, runs each pass over\n24: ///   a Function.\n25: /// * ModulePassManager must be directly run, runs each pass over the Module.\n26: ///\n27: /// Note that the implementations of the pass managers use concept-based\n28: /// polymorphism as outlined in the \"Value Semantics and Concept-based\n29: /// Polymorphism\" talk (or its abbreviated sibling \"Inheritance Is The Base\n30: /// Class of Evil\") by Sean Parent:\n31: /// * https://sean-parent.stlab.cc/papers-and-presentations\n32: /// * http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_BpMYeUFXv8\n33: /// * https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/shows/goingnative-2013/inheritance-base-class-of-evil\n34: ///\n35: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n36: \n37: #ifndef LLVM_IR_PASSMANAGER_H\n38: #define LLVM_IR_PASSMANAGER_H\n39: \n40: #include \"llvm/ADT/DenseMap.h\"\n41: #include \"llvm/ADT/STLExtras.h\"\n42: #include \"llvm/ADT/StringExtras.h\"\n43: #include \"llvm/ADT/StringRef.h\"\n44: #include \"llvm/ADT/TinyPtrVector.h\"\n45: #include \"llvm/IR/Analysis.h\"\n46: #include \"llvm/IR/PassManagerInternal.h\"\n47: #include \"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\"\n48: #include \"llvm/Support/TypeName.h\"\n49: #include <cassert>\n50: #include <cstring>\n51: #include <list>\n52: #include <memory>\n53: #include <tuple>\n54: #include <type_traits>\n55: #include <utility>\n56: #include <vector>\n57: \n58: namespace llvm {\n59: \n60: class Function;\n61: class Module;\n62: \n63: // Forward declare the analysis manager template.\n64: template <typename IRUnitT, typename... ExtraArgTs> class AnalysisManager;\n65: \n66: /// A CRTP mix-in to automatically provide informational APIs needed for\n67: /// passes.\n68: ///\n69: /// This provides some boilerplate for types that are passes.\n70: template <typename DerivedT> struct PassInfoMixin {\n71:   /// Gets the name of the pass we are mixed into.\n72:   static StringRef name() {\n73:     static_assert(std::is_base_of<PassInfoMixin, DerivedT>::value,\n74:                   \"Must pass the derived type as the template argument!\");\n75:     StringRef Name = getTypeName<DerivedT>();\n76:     Name.consume_front(\"llvm::\");\n77:     return Name;\n78:   }\n79: \n80:   void printPipeline(raw_ostream &OS,\n81:                      function_ref<StringRef(StringRef)> MapClassName2PassName) {\n82:     StringRef ClassName = DerivedT::name();\n83:     auto PassName = MapClassName2PassName(ClassName);\n84:     OS << PassName;\n85:   }\n86: };\n87: \n88: /// A CRTP mix-in that provides informational APIs needed for analysis passes.\n89: ///\n90: /// This provides some boilerplate for types that are analysis passes. It\n91: /// automatically mixes in \\c PassInfoMixin.\n92: template <typename DerivedT>\n93: struct AnalysisInfoMixin : PassInfoMixin<DerivedT> {\n94:   /// Returns an opaque, unique ID for this analysis type.\n95:   ///\n96:   /// This ID is a pointer type that is guaranteed to be 8-byte aligned and thus\n97:   /// suitable for use in sets, maps, and other data structures that use the low\n98:   /// bits of pointers.\n99:   ///\n100:   /// Note that this requires the derived type provide a static \\c AnalysisKey\n101:   /// member called \\c Key.\n102:   ///\n103:   /// FIXME: The only reason the mixin type itself can't declare the Key value\n104:   /// is that some compilers cannot correctly unique a templated static variable\n105:   /// so it has the same addresses in each instantiation. The only currently\n106:   /// known platform with this limitation is Windows DLL builds, specifically\n107:   /// building each part of LLVM as a DLL. If we ever remove that build\n108:   /// configuration, this mixin can provide the static key as well.\n109:   static AnalysisKey *ID() {\n110:     static_assert(std::is_base_of<AnalysisInfoMixin, DerivedT>::value,\n111:                   \"Must pass the derived type as the template argument!\");\n112:     return &DerivedT::Key;\n113:   }\n114: };\n115: \n116: namespace detail {\n117: \n118: /// Actual unpacker of extra arguments in getAnalysisResult,\n119: /// passes only those tuple arguments that are mentioned in index_sequence.\n120: template <typename PassT, typename IRUnitT, typename AnalysisManagerT,\n121:           typename... ArgTs, size_t... Ns>\n122: typename PassT::Result\n123: getAnalysisResultUnpackTuple(AnalysisManagerT &AM, IRUnitT &IR,\n124:                              std::tuple<ArgTs...> Args,\n125:                              std::index_sequence<Ns...>) {\n126:   (void)Args;\n127:   return AM.template getResult<PassT>(IR, std::get<Ns>(Args)...);\n128: }\n129: \n130: /// Helper for *partial* unpacking of extra arguments in getAnalysisResult.\n131: ///\n132: /// Arguments passed in tuple come from PassManager, so they might have extra\n133: /// arguments after those AnalysisManager's ExtraArgTs ones that we need to\n134: /// pass to getResult.\n135: template <typename PassT, typename IRUnitT, typename... AnalysisArgTs,\n136:           typename... MainArgTs>\n137: typename PassT::Result\n138: getAnalysisResult(AnalysisManager<IRUnitT, AnalysisArgTs...> &AM, IRUnitT &IR,\n139:                   std::tuple<MainArgTs...> Args) {\n140:   return (getAnalysisResultUnpackTuple<\n141:           PassT, IRUnitT>)(AM, IR, Args,\n142:                            std::index_sequence_for<AnalysisArgTs...>{});\n143: }\n144: \n145: } // namespace detail\n146: \n147: /// Manages a sequence of passes over a particular unit of IR.\n148: ///\n149: /// A pass manager contains a sequence of passes to run over a particular unit\n150: /// of IR (e.g. Functions, Modules). It\\n239:   /// uses cost modeling and thresholds to balance code growth against runtime\\n240:   /// improvements. It\\n256:   /// typically correspond to frontend \\\"-O[123]\\\" options for optimization\\n257:   /// levels \\\\c O1, \\\\c O2 and \\\\c O3 resp.\\n258:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager buildPerModuleDefaultPipeline(\\n259:       OptimizationLevel Level,\\n260:       ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase = ThinOrFullLTOPhase::None);\\n261: \\n262:   /// Build a fat object default optimization pipeline.\\n263:   ///\\n264:   /// This builds a pipeline that runs the LTO/ThinLTO  pre-link pipeline, and\\n265:   /// emits a section containing the pre-link bitcode along side the object code\\n266:   /// generated in non-LTO compilation.\\n267:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager buildFatLTODefaultPipeline(OptimizationLevel Level,\\n268:                                                         bool ThinLTO,\\n269:                                                         bool EmitSummary);\\n270: \\n271:   /// Build a pre-link, ThinLTO-targeting default optimization pipeline to\\n272:   /// a pass manager.\\n273:   ///\\n274:   /// This adds the pre-link optimizations tuned to prepare a module for\\n275:   /// a ThinLTO run. All passes\\n331:   /// are comma separated. As a special shortcut, if the very first pass is not\\n332:   /// a module pass (as a module pass manager is), this will automatically form\\n333:   /// the shortest stack of pass managers that allow inserting that first pass.\\n334:   /// So, assuming function passes 'fpassN', CGSCC passes 'cgpassN', and loop\\n335:   /// passes 'lpassN', all of these are valid:\\n336:   ///\\n337:   ///   fpass1,fpass2,fpass3\\n338:   ///   cgpass1,cgpass2,cgpass3\\n339:   ///   lpass1,lpass2,lpass3\\n340:   ///\\n341:   /// And they are equivalent to the following (resp.):\\n342:   ///\\n343:   ///   module(function(fpass1,fpass2,fpass3))\\n344:   ///   module(cgscc(cgpass1,cgpass2,cgpass3))\\n345:   ///   module(function(loop(lpass1,lpass2,lpass3)))\\n346:   ///\\n347:   /// This shortcut is especially useful for debugging and testing small pass\\n348:   /// combinations.\\n349:   ///\\n350:   /// The sequence of passes aren't necessarily the exact same kind of pass.\\n351:   /// You can mix different levels implicitly if adaptor passes are defined to\\n352:   /// make them work. For example,\\n353:   ///\\n354:   ///   mpass1,fpass1,fpass2,mpass2,lpass1\\n355:   ///\\n356:   /// This pipeline uses only one pass manager: the top-level module manager.\\n357:   /// fpass1,fpass2 and lpass1 are added into the top-level module manager\\n358:   /// using only adaptor passes. No nested function/loop pass managers are\\n359:   /// added. The purpose is to allow easy pass testing when the user\\n360:   /// specifically want the pass to run under a adaptor directly. This is\\n361:   /// preferred when a pipeline is largely of one type, but one or just a few\\n362:   /// passes are of different types(See PassBuilder.cpp for examples).\\n363:   LLVM_ABI Error parsePassPipeline(ModulePassManager &MPM,\\n364:                                    StringRef PipelineText);\\n365: \\n366:   /// {{@ Parse a textual pass pipeline description into a specific PassManager\\n367:   ///\\n368:   /// Automatic deduction of an appropriate pass manager stack is not supported.\\n369:   /// For example, to insert a loop pass 'lpass' into a FunctionPassManager,\\n370:   /// this is the valid pipeline text:\\n371:   ///\\n372:   ///   function(lpass)\\n373:   LLVM_ABI Error parsePassPipeline(CGSCCPassManager &CGPM,\\n374:                                    StringRef PipelineText);\\n375:   LLVM_ABI Error parsePassPipeline(FunctionPassManager &FPM,\\n376:                                    StringRef PipelineText);\\n377:   LLVM_ABI Error parsePassPipeline(LoopPassManager &LPM,\\n378:                                    StringRef PipelineText);\\n379:   /// @}}\\n380: \\n381:   /// Parse a textual MIR pipeline into the provided \\\\c MachineFunctionPass\\n382:   /// manager.\\n383:   /// The format of the textual machine pipeline is a comma separated list of\\n384:   /// machine pass names:\\n385:   ///\\n386:   ///   machine-funciton-pass,machine-module-pass,...\\n387:   ///\\n388:   /// There is no need to specify the pass nesting, and this function\\n389:   /// currently cannot handle the pass nesting.\\n390:   LLVM_ABI Error parsePassPipeline(MachineFunctionPassManager &MFPM,\\n391:                                    StringRef PipelineText);\\n392: \\n393:   /// Parse a textual alias analysis pipeline into Other optimizations which runs later might get benefit of no-alias\n1544:   // assumption in clone loop.\n1545:   if (UseLoopVersioningLICM) {\n1546:     OptimizePM.addPass(\n1547:         createFunctionToLoopPassAdaptor(LoopVersioningLICMPass()));\n1548:     // LoopVersioningLICM pass might increase new LICM opportunities.\n1549:     OptimizePM.addPass(createFunctionToLoopPassAdaptor(\n1550:         LICMPass(PTO.LicmMssaOptCap, PTO.LicmMssaNoAccForPromotionCap,\n1551:                  /*AllowSpeculation=*/true),\n1552:         /*USeMemorySSA=*/true));\n1553:   }\n1554: \n1555:   OptimizePM.addPass(Float2IntPass());\n1556:   OptimizePM.addPass(LowerConstantIntrinsicsPass());\n1557: \n1558:   if (EnableMatrix) {\n1559:     OptimizePM.addPass(LowerMatrixIntrinsicsPass());\n1560:     OptimizePM.addPass(EarlyCSEPass());\n1561:   }\n1562: \n1563:   // CHR pass should only be applied with the profile information.\n1564:   // The check is to check the profile summary information in CHR.\n1565:   if (EnableCHR && Level == OptimizationLevel::O3)\n1566:     OptimizePM.addPass(ControlHeightReductionPass());\n1567: \n1568:   // FIXME: We need to run some loop optimizations to re-rotate loops after\n1569:   // simplifycfg and others undo their rotation.\n1570: \n1571:   // Optimize the loop execution. These passes operate on entire loop nests\n1572:   // rather than on each loop in an inside-out manner, and so they are actually\n1573:   // function passes.\n1574: \n1575:   invokeVectorizerStartEPCallbacks(OptimizePM, Level);\n1576: \n1577:   LoopPassManager LPM;\n1578:   // First rotate loops that may have been un-rotated by prior passes.\n1579:   // Disable header duplication at -Oz.\n1580:   LPM.addPass(LoopRotatePass(EnableLoopHeaderDuplication ||\n1581:                                  Level != OptimizationLevel::Oz,\n1582:                              LTOPreLink));\n1583:   // Some loops may have become dead by now. Try to delete them.\n1584:   // FIXME: see discussion in https://reviews.llvm.org/D112851,\n1585:   //        this may need to be revisited once we run GVN before loop deletion\n1586:   //        in the simplification pipeline.\n1587:   LPM.addPass(LoopDeletionPass());\n1588: \n1589:   if (PTO.LoopInterchange)\n1590:     LPM.addPass(LoopInterchangePass());\n1591: \n1592:   OptimizePM.addPass(\n1593:       createFunctionToLoopPassAdaptor(std::move(LPM), /*UseMemorySSA=*/false));\n1594: \n1595:   // FIXME: This may not be the right place in the pipeline.\n1596:   // We need to have the data to support the right place.\n1597:   if (PTO.LoopFusion)\n1598:     OptimizePM.addPass(LoopFusePass());\n1599: \n1600:   // Distribute loops to allow partial vectorization.  I.e. isolate dependences\n1601: ",

LLVM Pass Manager Registration and Execution Chain\\n\\n### Overview\\nLLVM's optimization pass system uses a sophisticated chain of components to register, manage, and execute transformation passes. This trace covers both the legacy pass manager and the new pass manager (NPM) infrastructure.\\n\\n### 1. Pass Manager Template (llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h)\\nThe core PassManager is a template class that manages a sequence of passes over a particular unit of IR (Module, Function, Loop, etc.). Key aspects:\\n- **Template Definition** (lines 159-226): `template <typename IRUnitT, typename AnalysisManagerT = AnalysisManager<IRUnitT>, typename... ExtraArgTs> class PassManager`\\n- **addPass() Method** (lines 193-214): Adds passes to the manager using concept-based polymorphism, storing them in a vector of unique_ptr<PassConceptT>\\n- **run() Method** (lines 188-191): Declared here, implemented in PassManagerImpl.h\\n- **Type Aliases**: ModulePassManager (line 238), FunctionPassManager (line 247)\\n\\n### 2. Key components:\\n- **getPassRegistry()** (line 58): Returns the global registry object initialized at application startup\\n- **registerPass()** (line 70): Registers a pass (by PassInfo) with the registry, required for use with PassManager\\n- **getPassInfo()** (lines 62, 66): Looks up a pass's PassInfo by type identifier or argument string\\n- **PassInfoMap** (line 43): DenseMap storing PassInfo objects indexed by pass type pointer\\n- **PassInfoStringMap** (line 45): StringMap for lookup by command-line argument\\n\\n### 3. Pass Registration Macros (llvm/include/llvm/PassSupport.h)\\nThe registration system uses macros to automate pass setup:\\n- **INITIALIZE_PASS_BEGIN/END** (lines 39-54): Macro pair that creates initialization functions and PassInfo objects\\n  - Creates `initialize<PassName>PassOnce()` function containing registration code\\n  - Defines `PassInfo` with pass name, argument, ID, constructor function, and analysis flags\\n  - Calls `Registry.registerPass(*PI, true)` to register the pass\\n  - Uses `llvm::once_flag` for thread-safe initialization (lines 50-54)\\n- **INITIALIZE_PASS_DEPENDENCY** (line 42): Declares pass dependencies during initialization\\n- **RegisterPass Template** (lines 89-98): Alternative registration mechanism for simple cases\\n  - Inherits from PassInfo\\n  - Calls `PassRegistry::getPassRegistry()->registerPass(*this)` in constructor\\n\\nExample from llvm/lib/Transforms/InstCombine/InstructionCombining.cpp (lines 6331-6343):\\n```cpp\\nINITIALIZE_PASS_BEGIN(InstructionCombiningPass, \\\"instcombine\\\",\\n                      \\\"Combine redundant instructions\\\", false, false)\\nINITIALIZE_PASS_DEPENDENCY(AssumptionCacheTracker)\\nINITIALIZE_PASS_DEPENDENCY(TargetLibraryInfoWrapperPass)\\nINITIALIZE_PASS_END(InstructionCombiningPass, \\\"instcombine\\\",\\n                    \\\"Combine redundant instructions\\\", false, false)\\n```\\n\\n### 4. Scalar optimizations\\n- `initializeVectorization()` - Vectorization passes\\n- `initializeInstCombine()` - InstCombine pass\\n- `initializeIPO()` - Inter-procedural optimizations\\n- Individual pass initialization functions like `initializeInstructionCombiningPassPass()`\\n\\n### Key Execution Chain\\n\\n1. **Registration Phase** (at startup):\\n   -
